вқҜ /speckit-specify Alright, now our goal is to start building the actual agent  
using spec-kit as before. Go through what has been done before. Now we want to  
convert the POC (that I wrote under pocs/changepoint) into the full agent core  
code.                                                                           
                                                                                
We need to modularize it keeping in mind two things:                            
1. We should be able to do a lift-and-shit (to possibly an MCP server) of the   
tools that we define for the agent                                              
2. Every stage in the Agent Analysis should fire out JSON payloads to the UI    
app so that we can visualize what is happening on the UI (we will drill down on 
the details on this in due course)                                              
3. We need a config file (config.yaml) that captures the following              
a. Agent model IDs : VISUAL_MODEL_ID, REACT_MODEL_ID - In the POC code, these   
are in .env, we need to shift this to the config file. We can retain the same   
defaults for these.                                                             
b. A boolean switch that determines if visual node/analysis is enabled          
(Default: True) - lets call it VISUAL_ANALYSIS_ENABLED                          
c. A `diagnostics` section that lists everything present in the diagnostic      
bundle (DiagnosticsBundle) - I can turn on and off and figure out if some       
statistical information is really useful or is it just polluting the context    
for the agent. The default value is true for all the diagnostics.               
d. An `agent_tools` section that lists the tools available to the agent - as    
before, I can enable/disable certain tools to figure out its efficacies. The    
default value is true for all the tools.                                        
4. Train/Validation/Test set ratios                                             
                                                                                
                                                                                
                                                                                
The idea behind the config file is that:                                        
1. The UI will read the config file and display those in the UI for us to       
check/uncheck. Whenever we trigger the agent with those specific                
checked/unchecked config, it should take effect and the entire agent code       
should behave in the configured way. So this means the backend should have      
appropriate hooks that reads stuff from a working config file and applies the   
workflows accordingly                                                           
                                                                                
I have attached a screenshot of an in-development version of the UI (the repo   
itself has it it was developed by Sowmya) for reference - Sowmya will expand on 
this in the coming days.

вҸә I've now read the full changepoint POC (pocs/changepoint/), the prior spec
  (003-changepoint-agent-poc), the constitution, SPEC.md, the empty
  src/ailf/core + pipeline skeletons, the existing drift Streamlit app, and the
  UI screenshot. Here's my understanding before we write anything.

  What the POC actually is

  A working LangGraph agent for changepoint forecasting, in these modules:

  - config.py вҖ” env-driven (VISUAL_MODEL_ID, REACT_MODEL_ID, AWS_REGION, seed,
  LangSmith)
  - scenarios.py вҖ” loads CSV fixtures + scenario_metadata.json, builds
  SeriesSplit (train/val/test by absolute train_end / validation_horizon /
  test_horizon)
  - detector.py вҖ” deterministic Prophet changepoint detection
  - diagnostics.py вҖ” the DiagnosticsBundle (12 statistical fields:
  detected/latest/primary changepoints, segment stats, event blocks,
  recurring-event summary, drift intervals, transient/permanent scores, вҖҰ)
  - interventions.py вҖ” the bounded 5-tool menu (recent_window, step, ramp,
  clean_event, holidays-tuned) + validation/test evaluation вҖ” this is what you 
  mean by "the tools"
  - graph/ вҖ” state + nodes: visual вҲҘ diagnostics вҶ’ decision вҶ” validation вҶ’ final
  - baselines.py, forecasting.py, viz.py, reporting.py, run_poc.py

  How I read the conversion (defaults I'll assume unless you correct me)

  Scope: Promote this POC into the review-gated src/ailf/core/ (generic,
  serializable, test-first per the constitution) + a thin
  src/ailf/pipelines/changepoint/, with changepoint as the first/reference
  pipeline. The other two tracks plug in later.

  Core vs. pipeline split (per your CLAUDE.md repo map):
  - Core (shared): the graph/ReAct engine, the tool-registry mechanism, the
  backtest/validation gate, metrics, the model wrapper, the stage-event 
  emission, the config loader, reporting.
  - Changepoint pipeline (thin): the detector, the DiagnosticsBundle, the 5
  interventions, versioned prompts, fixtures, and pipeline.py wiring.

  Other defaults I'll bake in (tell me if wrong):
  - Secrets (Anthropic key, AWS creds) stay in .env; non-secret operational
  settings (model IDs, region, LangSmith toggle, VISUAL_ANALYSIS_ENABLED,
  diagnostics, agent_tools, split ratios) move to config.yaml at repo root.
  - UI events: each stage emits a typed, serializable event (stage, status: 
  start|complete, payload) through an emitter abstraction the core calls;
  concrete transport (SSE/WebSocket/file) is deferred ("we'll drill down later")
  вҖ” the spec just fixes the interface and per-stage payload shape.
  - VISUAL_ANALYSIS_ENABLED=false вҶ’ skip the visual node; decision runs on a
  diagnostics-only versioned prompt; the visual-first ordering invariant is
  relaxed for that mode; trace records it.
  - A guaranteed-valid fallback (full-history Prophet) always remains so a run
  yields an agent forecast even if toggles remove every structural tool.

  Four decisions genuinely change the spec, and I don't want to assume them:

вҸә All four decisions are locked. Let me restate the full decision set so the
  spec is built on exactly this:

  1. Tools вҖ” menu-select + relocatable: agent proposes one intervention via
  structured output; the deterministic backtest gate scores it; each
  intervention sits behind a serializable registry contract so it can later be
  served over MCP. No free-form tool-calling; agent never sees scores mid-loop.
  2. Config delivery вҖ” per-run override merged with config.yaml defaults; the
  resolved config is recorded with the run's artifacts.
  3. Split units вҖ” golden absolute split stays in metadata as the per-scenario
  default; a run may override with either ratios or absolute row counts.
  4. Toggles вҖ” disabled diagnostics are still computed but hidden from the 
  agent; disabled tools are removed from the menu; the trace records what was
  hidden/removed.

  Let me run the spec-kit pre-execution checks (hooks + numbering) before
  authoring.

  ---
  Question 1 of ~4 вҖ” Unit of execution ("a run")

  Context: The POC runs all five scenarios in one batch invocation and writes a
  cross-scenario summary.md. But the UI screenshot shows selecting one series
  and clicking "Detect & Forecast", and your new requirements attach config
  overrides and the event stream to "a run". So the spec currently carries both
  models вҖ” the per-run config/events language (US2, US5) and the cross-scenario
  summary (FR-035, SC-001). I need to know what "a run" is, because config
  scope, event scope, and the artifact set all attach to it.

  Recommended: Option A вҖ” it matches the UI's single-series trigger, makes the
  per-run config/event/artifact scoping unambiguous, and keeps the batch summary
  alive as a thin wrapper (so nothing is lost) without making batch the primary
  unit.

  Option: A
  Description: A run = one series/scenario. The UI (and core entrypoint)
  triggers
     single-series runs; per-run config override, the event stream, and
  artifacts
     all scope to that one series. The cross-scenario summary becomes an
  optional
     batch wrapper that invokes N single runs and aggregates their results (kept

    as a dev/eval convenience,  not the primary unit).
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Option: B
  Description: A run = the full batch over all scenarios (POC model). One
    effective config and one event stream span all scenarios; the cross-scenario

    summary is the primary artifact. The UI triggering one series is just a
    filtered batch of size 1.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Option: C
  Description: Both first-class. A single-series run and a batch run are
  distinct
     top-level operations; a batch run is composed of single runs that  share
  one
     resolved effective config, each still emitting its own per-series events
  and
     artifacts.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  You can reply with the option letter (e.g., "A"), accept the recommendation by
  saying "yes" or "recommended", or provide your own short answer.

  ---
  Question 2 of ~4 вҖ” Run-failure policy for the event stream

  Context: FR-032 says a stage failure emits an error event "and the run
  terminates or degrades per the documented policy" вҖ” but the policy itself is
  undefined. The POC raised hard (e.g., ModelUnavailableError,
  InterventionError). This matters because the UI consuming the event stream
  needs to know whether a failed stage ends the run or whether the run continues
  in a degraded mode, and the implementation/tests branch on it.

  Recommended: Option A вҖ” it matches the POC's fail-fast, no-silent-fallback
  ethos and the constitution's honesty principles, keeps the event contract
  simple (an error event is always terminal), and avoids the agent producing a
  result from a half-broken pipeline. The few places the POC already degrades
  gracefully (a rejected/out-of-bounds proposal, or exhausting the iteration
  budget) are normal in-loop control flow, not stage failures, so they stay as
  they are.

  Option: A
  Description: Fail-fast: a stage error terminates the run. Any stage that
  raises
     emits a terminal error event and the run stops; no partial/degraded agent
    forecast is produced. Existing in-loop control flow (proposal rejected,
    bounds violation, budget exhausted вҶ’ carry best-validation proposal) is
    normal flow, not a stage failure, and is unaffected.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Option: B
  Description: Degrade where safe, terminate otherwise. Define which stages are
    recoverable (e.g., visual-inspection failure вҶ’ fall back to diagnostics-only

    and continue) vs. fatal (config, split, final evaluation). More resilient,
    but adds per-stage policy the spec and tests must enumerate.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Option: C
  Description: Always continue and report. Every stage error is emitted but the
    run pushes on with whatever it has, surfacing a degraded result. Maximizes
    liveness for the UI demo, weakest correctness guarantee.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

вҸә Question 2 fully integrated. Now there's a knock-on edge case worth adding to

  ---
  Question 3 of ~4 вҖ” Concurrency model for runs

  Context: The spec repeatedly says "concurrent runs may use different configs"
  and "runs are isolated" (US2 clarification, Assumptions), and the UI is a
  triggered-run model. But it never states whether the backend must actually
  support concurrent runs in this feature, or merely not preclude them. This
  materially affects the design: true concurrency forces per-run isolation of
  global state (the POC sets process-wide random.seed/np.random.seed and uses
  module-level Prophet logging config), whereas "one run at a time" lets that
  slide for now.

  Recommended: Option B вҖ” the constitution's reproducibility principle (fixed,
  recorded seeds) and the POC's reliance on process-global seeding make true
  in-process parallelism a real correctness hazard that's out of proportion to
  this feature's goal. Designing the interfaces to be isolation-ready (per-run
  config object, per-run artifact dir, no shared mutable config) while only
  guaranteeing serial execution now keeps the door open for the UI/transport
  feature to add a job queue without a redesign.

  Option: A
  Description: Must support concurrent in-process runs. The core must safely run

    multiple scenarios in parallel within one process вҖ” no shared mutable state,

    per-run seeding, thread/async-safe emitter. Strongest, but forces removing
    the POC's process-global seed/logging patterns now and concurrency tests.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Option: B
  Description: Isolation-ready, serial execution guaranteed. Interfaces are
    designed for isolation (per-run effective config, per-run artifact  dir,
    per-run event stream, no shared mutable config) but the feature only
    guarantees one run at a time; a later transport/queue  feature can add
    parallelism without redesign. Per-run reproducibility (seed recorded per
  run)
     is guaranteed regardless.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Option: C
  Description: Single-run only, no isolation claims. Drop the "concurrent runs"
    language; assume one run per process invocation, like the POC. Simplest, but

    the spec's isolation wording would be removed and the UI couldn't fan out
    later without revisiting the core.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Option: Short
  Description: Provide a different short answer (вүӨ5 words)

  You can reply with the option letter (e.g., "A"), accept the recommendation by
  saying "yes" or "recommended", or provide your own short answer.

  ---
  Question 4 of ~4 вҖ” Scope of the event-emitting stages

  Context: FR-026/FR-027 require "every stage" to emit events, and the POC's
  deterministic pre-agent steps (changepoint detection, baseline fitting) happen
  outside the LangGraph graph in run_poc.py вҖ” they aren't graph "stages" today.
  The spec lists "configuration resolved, split built, diagnostics computed,
  visual inspection, decision iterations, validation, final evaluation, run
  complete" (FR-027) but is silent on the deterministic detector and the two
  baseline fits. The UI screenshot shows changepoints and the forecast
  comparison prominently, so whether those steps emit events affects what the UI
  can render live and what the event contract must cover.

  Recommended: Option A вҖ” the UI screenshot foregrounds detected changepoints
  and the baseline-vs-agent comparison, so emitting events for detection and
  baseline fitting is what makes those panels live rather than only-at-the-end;
  it also keeps "every stage emits" literally true. The cost is small (a few
  more documented payload shapes).

  Option: A
  Description: Emit for all run steps, deterministic ones included. Changepoint
    detection and the two baseline fits (full-history Prophet, naive-window
    workflow) each emit start/complete events with their results, alongside the
    agent stages. The event contract covers the  whole run, matching what the UI

    screenshot displays (changepoints, baseline comparison).
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Option: B
  Description: Agent-graph stages only. Events cover just the graph stages
    enumerated in FR-027 (visual, diagnostics, decision, validation, final).
    Detection and baseline fits remain pre-agent setup with no  events; the UI
    derives them from the final artifacts instead of live events. Smaller
    contract, less live detail.

       19 +driven by a pipeline-owned `config.yaml` (model IDs, `visual_a
          +nalysis_enabled`, per-diagnostic and                          
       20 +per-tool toggles, split knobs) plus an optional per-run overri
          +de that is merged, validated, and                             
       21 +recorded. The deciding constraint is **POC parity** (SC-001): 
          +the deterministic baseline and                                
       22 +validation metrics must match the POC bit-for-bit for the comm
          +itted fixtures and seed.

       77  
       41 -*GATE: Must pass before Phase 0 research. Re-check after Phase

       79  
       43 -[Gates determined based on constitution file]                 
       80 +The POC exemption **no longer applies** вҖ” this code enters `sr
          +c/ailf/core` and a promoted pipeline, so                      
       81 +all gates bind. The design satisfies them, with three deviatio
          +ns justified in writing below.                                
       82  
       83 +| Principle | Status | How this plan honors it |              
       84 +|-----------|--------|--------------------------|             
       85 +| **I. Importable Core (serializable boundary)** | **PASS** | 
          +All core public I/O is plain frozen dataclasses with `to_dict`
          +/`from_dict` (mirroring `core/datasets/case.py`) or plain dict
          +s. `langgraph` is confined to `core/agent/engine.py`; `langcha
          +in_aws` to `core/models/llm.py`; import-guard tests enforce bo
          +th and assert importing `core.backtest`/`core.agent`/`core.eve
          +nts` does **not** transitively import the Darts-coupled `core.
          +datasets`. A single `to_json` chokepoint raises on non-JSON ty
          +pes (numpy, `pd.Timestamp`, model handles), replacing the POC'
          +s lossy `default=str`. |                                      
       86 +| **II. Test-First (NON-NEGOTIABLE)** | **PASS (w/ scoped-out 
          +metrics вҖ” see Deviation 1)** | Every deterministic unit (confi
          +g resolver, split resolver, registry + bounds gate, metrics, e
          +vent emitter + sink, detector, diagnostics, baselines, validat
          +ion scoring) is built failing-then-passing. Diagnostic tools g
          +et KNOWN-injected-ground-truth precision/recall/FPR tests. |  
       87 +| **III. Golden-set Evaluation** | **PASS** | The LLM visual/d
          +ecision stages are excluded from exact-output unit tests; cove
          +red by trace-invariant + leakage-invariant tests (FakeModelWra
          +pper) and an opt-in golden-set eval (tool-family vs `expected_
          +intervention_family`). The two agent-affecting changes (new de
          +cision prompt version, generated menu) require a **documented 
          +before/after golden-set capture with sign-off** (see Deviation
          + 3 handling). |                                               
       88 +| **IV. Bounded Interventions, Backtest-Gated (NON-NEGOTIABLE)
          +** | **PASS (single-holdout вҖ” see Deviation 2)** | Fixed five-
          +tool menu + bounded grids declared once as `ToolSpec` allowed-
          +values; the gate is the sole authority; acceptance requires st
          +rictly beating the naive baseline on a historical holdout; hid
          +den test only at final evaluation; the agent proposes, the gua
          +rdrail disposes. |                                            
       89 +| **V. Reproducible & Honest Evaluation** | **PASS** | `uv` + 
          +committed lock; `prophet` pinned; seed `1729` applied as the f
          +irst prelude step and recorded in `effective_config.json` + `S
          +plitProvenance`; naive-window workflow is the honest comparato
          +r; `metrics.json` reports MAE/RMSE/WAPE/sMAPE for all three me
          +thods. |                                                      
       90 +| **VI. Transparent, Explainable Outputs** | **PASS (narrative
          + report added)** | Beyond `agent_trace.json` + `metrics.json` 
          ++ plots, a per-run `report.md` (core/reporting) covers dataset
          +/horizon, baseline comparison, detected issues, the accepted/b
          +est-val intervention with **before/after metric deltas vs naiv
          +e**, the final recommendation, and the agent's stated limitati
          +ons. The agent's reasoning and every accept/reject decision ar
          +e inspectable. |                                              
       91 +| **VII. Shared Core, Independent Pipelines** | **PASS** | Gen
          +eric spine in `core/`; changepoint leaf in `pipelines/changepo
          +int/` importing only `core` + stdlib (import-cleanliness test)
          +. Core holds zero changepoint/Prophet/UI symbols (SC-002). The
          + pipeline injects the diagnostics field-set and structural too
          +l-name set into the core validator so core stays use-case-agno
          +stic. |                                                       
       92 +                                                              
       93 +**Per-change gates**: deterministic logic test-first вң… В· agen
          +t-affecting changes golden-gated (documented capture) вң… В· int
          +erventions bounds-checked + backtest-gated вң… В· run emits a co
          +mplete explanation report вң… В· `uv` lock current + `prophet` p
          +inned вң… В· core touched вҶ’ extra review + core tests green вң…. 
       94 +                                                              
       95 +### Deviations justified in writing (Governance: deviations mu
          +st be justified)                                              
       96 +                                                              
       97 +1. **MASE and prediction-interval coverage are scoped OUT of t
          +his feature.** Principle II enumerates                        
       98 +   MASE and PI-coverage among project metrics. This promotion 
          +is **behavior-preserving** вҖ” its SC-001                       
       99 +   is bit-parity with the POC, which computes only MAE (primar
          +y) / RMSE / WAPE / sMAPE вҖ” and no FR or                       
      100 +   SC of this feature references MASE or PI-coverage. Principl
          +e II governs *how* metrics are built                          
      101 +   (test-first) when built, not that every feature implements 
          +the full menu. `core/metrics/metrics.py`                      
      102 +   is structured so MASE and PI-coverage can be added later te
          +st-first (a `metrics()` extension point);                     
      103 +   adding them now would introduce un-asserted quantities and 
          +risk the parity oracle. **Resolution:                         
      104 +   defer, with the metrics module shaped to accept them.** (Re
          +corded in Complexity Tracking.)                               
      105 +                                                              
      106 +2. **The gate uses a single validation holdout, not a rolling-
          +origin backtest.** Principles IV/V and                        
      107 +   the `core/backtest/__init__.py` stub say "rolling-origin." 
          +The promoted gate preserves the POC's                         
      108 +   single-holdout protocol (the last `validation_horizon` bloc
          +k of training), which the prior POC spec                      
      109 +   documented and the POC exemption permitted. To avoid a core
          + symbol whose contract contradicts its                        
      110 +   behavior (SC-002 "verifiable by inspection"), the module is
          + named and documented honestly as a                           
      111 +   **single validation-holdout gate**, and the `core/backtest/
          +__init__.py` docstring is corrected to                        
      112 +   say rolling-origin is a future extension. **Resolution: hon
          +est naming + written justification;                           
      113 +   rolling-origin deferred to a later core feature** when drif
          +t/anomaly need it.                                            
      114 +                                                              
      115 +3. **Two agent-affecting changes ship (new versioned decision 
          +prompt + generated menu).** Principle                         
      116 +   III forbids unjustified agent regressions. The deterministi
          +c suite asserts the structural                                
      117 +   invariants (visual-first ordering when enabled, leakage, me
          +nu pruning on toggle) via FakeModelWrapper;                   
      118 +   the **semantic** no-regression bar is enforced by a documen
          +ted golden-set capture before/after the                       
      119 +   change (tool-family vs `expected_intervention_family` acros
          +s the five scenarios) recorded in the PR.                     
      120 +   This keeps Principle III met without making Bedrock credent
          +ials a hard CI dependency.                                    
      121 +                                                              
      122 +**Gate result: PASS.** No unjustified violations. Complexity T
          +racking records the scoped-out items.                         
      123 +

      29 +def load_metadata() -> dict[str, Any]:                         
      30 +    if not _METADATA_PATH.exists():                            
      31 +        raise ScenarioError(f"Scenario metadata not found at {_
         +METADATA_PATH}")                                               
      32 +    return json.loads(_METADATA_PATH.read_text())

         +asename under this pipeline."""

      42 +        raise ScenarioError(f"{path} must have columns ds,y; go
         +t {list(frame.columns)}")

         +t) -> ResolvedSplit:

вҸә The values match to 4 decimals вҖ” changepoint indices identical, MAEs

       45 +    """Render the enabled-tools menu for the decision prompt's
          + {{tool_menu}} placeholder."""

          +etrics"],

      246 +    artifacts = [p.name for p in sorted(run_dir.glob("*")) if 
          +p.is_file()]

      254            f"run_dir={run_dir}")
      255      return metrics_report
